google_ads;




if(google_ads.length
!=
0)
{








apply_ad_config(google_ads.length);









render_ads(true,
window['ad_config_top']);









if(window['backfillParam'])
{












window['backfillParam']['pl_rnum']
=
google_ads.length;












window['backfillParam']['pl_time']
=
Date.now()
-
afc_ad_start_time;








}




}
}

function
apply_ad_config(num)
{
window['ad_config_top']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
window['ad_config_bot']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
}

google_ad_client
=
'ca-aj-cat';
google_ad_channel
=
'cx_ask_wiki,ad_dirN';
google_ad_output
=
'js';
google_max_num_ads
=
'4';
google_ad_type
=
'text';
google_image_size
=
'';
google_num_ads_recieved=
'';
google_language
=
'';
google_country
=
'';
google_encoding
=
'utf8';
google_safe
=
'medium';
google_adtest
=
'off';
google_ad_section
=
'default';
google_page_url
=
'';
google_hints
=
'Fat_Joe';
google_kw
=
'';
google_kw_type
=
'broad';


var
backfillParam
=
{




pl_rqnum
:
google_max_num_ads,




pl_hints
:
google_hints,




pl_rp
:
"false",




pl_kw
:
google_kw,




pl_cl
:
google_ad_client,




pl_ch
:
google_ad_channel,




pl_hex
:
"#FDFEEE",




pl_type
:
"afc",




pl_clksp
:
"none"};

var
word_arr
;

var
word_arr_len
;


function
highlightQuery(input_str)
{

var
queryTokenArray
=
"joe,fat,_,";


var
tok_arr
=
queryTokenArray.split(",");

for(tok_arr_idx=0;
tok_arr_idx
<
tok_arr.length-1;
tok_arr_idx
++)
{

if(isCombinationWord(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx])){
word_arr
=
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].split("-");
word_arr_len
=
word_arr.length;
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],0);

if(first_pos
!=-1)
{
input_str
=
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos);
}
}
else
{
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],0);
if(first_pos
!=
-1
&&
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].length
>
0)
{
input_str
=
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],first_pos);
}
}
}
return
input_str;
}

function
isCombinationWord(word){
if(word.indexOf("-")
!=
-1){
return
true;
}
else
{
return
false;
}
}


function
isAlpha(ch)
{
if
(ch
!=
null
&&
ch.match(/^[a-zA-Z0-9]+$/)){
return
true;
}
return
false;
}

function
isQueryinInput(firstindex,
input_str,
j){
for(i=firstindex;
i<
input_str.length
;
++i)
{
var
currindex
=
i;

if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(i)))
{
if(firstindex
==
currindex)

{
firstindex++;
}
else
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
if
(j
==
word_arr_len-1)
return
currindex;
else
return
isQueryinInput(currindex+1,input_str,++j);
}
}
}

if(j
<
word_arr_len)
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex+1).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
}

return
(currindex
+
1)
;
}


function

highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos)
{
exactmatch
=
isQueryinInput(first_pos+word_arr[0].length,input_str,1)
;
if(exactmatch
!=-1
)

{
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,exactmatch)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(exactmatch);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],exactmatch+7);
while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,next_pos);
}
}
return
input_str;
}


function

highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,
first_pos)
{
var
end_pos
=
first_pos
+
token.length;
if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(end_pos))
&&
!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(first_pos-1))){
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,end_pos)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(end_pos);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos+7);
}
else
{
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos);
}

while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,next_pos);
}
return
input_str;
}</script>

<p><b>Joseph
Antonio
Cartagena</b>
(born
August
19,
1970),
better
known
by
his
<a
href="/wiki/Stage_name?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stage
name">stage
name</a>
<b>Fat
Joe</b>,
is
an
American
<a
href="/wiki/Rapper?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rapper"
class="mw-redirect">rapper</a>.
He
is
also
the
CEO
of
<a
href="/wiki/Terror_Squad_Entertainment?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Terror
Squad
Entertainment">Terror
Squad
Entertainment</a>,
and
member
of
musical
groups
D.I.T.C.
and
Terror
Squad.</p>








<p>Fat
Joe's
first
album
was
<i><a
href="/wiki/Represent_(Fat_Joe_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Represent
(Fat
Joe
album)">Represent</a></i>,
released
in
1993,
followed
by
<i><a
href="/wiki/Jealous_One%27s_Envy?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jealous
One's
Envy">Jealous
One's
Envy</a></i>
in
1995.
From
1998
to
2006,
he
was
signed
to
<a
href="/wiki/Atlantic_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Atlantic
Records">Atlantic
Records</a>,
releasing
four
albums
under
the
label,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Don_Cartagena?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Don
Cartagena">Don
Cartagena</a></i>
in
1998,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Jealous_Ones_Still_Envy_(J.O.S.E.)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jealous
Ones
Still
Envy
(J.O.S.E.)">Jealous
Ones
Still
Envy
(J.O.S.E.)</a></i>
in
2001,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Loyalty_(Fat_Joe_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Loyalty
(Fat
Joe
album)">Loyalty</a></i>
in
2002,
and
<i><a
href="/wiki/All_or_Nothing_(Fat_Joe_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="All
or
Nothing
(Fat
Joe
album)">All
or
Nothing</a></i>
in
2005.<sup
id="cite_ref-all_music_1-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-all_music-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup>
Around
the
release
of
<i>All
or
Nothing</i>,
Fat
Joe
became
involved
in
a
highly
publicized
feud
with
another
New
York
City-based
rapper
<a
href="/wiki/50_Cent?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="50
Cent">50
Cent</a>,
who
attacked
Fat
Joe
in
his
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Piggy_Bank_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Piggy
Bank
(song)">Piggy
Bank</a>&quot;.
His
most
popular
song
in
which
he
performed
was
his
<a
href="/wiki/Remy_Ma?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Remy
Ma">Remy
Ma</a>
duet
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Lean_Back?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lean
Back">Lean
Back</a>&quot;
with
<a
href="/wiki/Terror_Squad_(group)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Terror
Squad
(group)">Terror
Squad</a>.
The
song
was
a
<a
href="/wiki/Hot_100_number-one_hits_of_2004_(USA)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hot
100
number-one
hits
of
2004
(USA)"
class="mw-redirect">number-one
hit
in
the
summer
of
2004</a>.</p>








<p>Starting
in
2006,
when
his
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Me,_Myself_%26_I_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"

&amp;

(album)">Me,
Myself,
&amp;
I</a></i>
was
released,

Joe
was

to
<a
href="/wiki/Imperial_Records?qsrc=3044"

Records</a>,

Entertainment">Terror
Squad
Entertainment</a>.

follow
up
album
was<i><a

Elephant
in
the
Room">The
Elephant
in
the
Room</a></i>,
which
was
released
in
2008;
<i><a
href="/wiki/Jealous_Ones_Still_Envy_2_(J.O.S.E._2)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jealous
Ones
Still
Envy
2
(J.O.S.E.
2)">Jealous
Ones
Still
Envy

(J.O.S.E.

the

<i><a

onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"

<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Early_life">Early
life</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Fat_Joe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1"
title="Edit
section:
Early
life">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>Fat
Joe
was
born
on
August
19,
1970
in
the
southern
<a
href="/wiki/Bronx?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bronx"
class="mw-redirect">Bronx</a>
area
of
<a
href="/wiki/New_York_City?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="New
York
City">New
York
City</a>,
where
he
was
raised
by
parents
of
<a
href="/wiki/Stateside_Puerto_Rican?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stateside
Puerto
Rican"
class="mw-redirect">Puerto
Rican</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Cuban_American?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cuban
American">Cuban</a>
descent.<sup
id="cite_ref-all_music_1-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-all_music-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
lived
in
<a
href="/wiki/Public_housing?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Public
housing">public
housing</a>
and
began
stealing
at
a
young
age
to
support
his
family.<sup
id="cite_ref-LatinRappin_5-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-LatinRappin-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
also
admits
that
he
was
a
<a
href="/wiki/Bullying?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bullying">bully</a>
in
his
childhood.<sup
id="cite_ref-LatinRappin_5-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-LatinRappin-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup>
His
brother
introduced
him
to
rap
music.
As
a
teenager,
he
was
highly
influenced
by
fellow
<a
href="/wiki/Latino?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Latino"
class="mw-redirect">Latino</a>
rapper
<a
href="/wiki/Big_Pun?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Big
Pun">Big
Pun</a>.
Fat
Joe
explained
the
rapper's
influence
on
him
by
saying
&quot;Latinos
before
us
who
had
the
opportunity
to
do
it
just
didn't
know
how
to
do
it.
They
came
in
trying
to
do
this
black
music,
waving
flags.
[But]
we're
trying
to
kick
in
the
doors
for
other
Latinos
and
represent
our
people,
and
it
shows.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-ChicagoTribune_6-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-ChicagoTribune-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Music_career">Music
career</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Fat_Joe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2"
title="Edit
section:
Music
career">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="1992.E2.80.931995:_Early_years">1992â€“1995:
Early
years</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Fat_Joe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3"
title="Edit
section:
1992â€“1995:
Early
years">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Under
stage
name
Fat
Joe
da
Gangsta
and
part
of
the
Diggin'
in
the
Crates
(<a
href="/wiki/D.I.T.C.?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="D.I.T.C."
class="mw-redirect">D.I.T.C.</a>)
rap
group,
Cartagena
was
signed
to
Relativity
Records
in
the
early
1990s,
recording
material
and
working
with
many
artists
who
he
would
later
sign
to
his
own
label.
In
1993,
his
debut
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Represent_(Fat_Joe_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Represent
(Fat
Joe
album)">Represent</a></i>,
was
released,
featuring
production
from
<a
href="/wiki/The_Beatnuts?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Beatnuts">The
Beatnuts</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Diamond_D?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Diamond
D">Diamond
D</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Lord_Finesse?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lord
Finesse">Lord
Finesse</a>,
and
others.
Its
lead
single,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Flow_Joe?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Flow
Joe">Flow
Joe</a>&quot;
peaked
at
number
one
on
the
Billboard
Hot
Rap
Singles
chart;
other
minor
singles
from
the
album
included
&quot;Watch
the
Sound&quot;
and
&quot;This
Shit
is
Real&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-all_music_1-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-all_music-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
1995,
Fat
Joe
released
his
second
studio
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Jealous_One%27s_Envy?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jealous
One's
Envy">Jealous
One's
Envy</a></i>,
which
peaked
at
#71
on
The
Billboard
200
and
at
#7
on
Top
R&amp;B/Hip
Hop
Albums.
The
album
featured
a
guest
appearance
from
KRS-One
and
production
from
Diamond
D.
The
lead
single
was
Success,
which
did
not
chart,
but
his
second
single,
&quot;Envy&quot;
peaked
at
#8
on
the
Hot
Rap
Tracks
chart.
The
success
of
this
album
led
Fat
Joe
to
be
featured
on
the
remix
of
<a
href="/wiki/LL_Cool_J?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="LL
Cool
J">LL
Cool
J</a>'s
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/I_Shot_Ya?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I
Shot
Ya"
class="mw-redirect">I
Shot
Ya</a>&quot;
along
with
<a
href="/wiki/Foxy_Brown_(rapper)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Foxy
Brown
(rapper)">Foxy
Brown</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Keith_Murray_(rapper)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Keith
Murray
(rapper)">Keith
Murray</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Prodigy_(rapper)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Prodigy
(rapper)">Prodigy</a>
of
<a
href="/wiki/Mobb_Deep?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mobb
Deep">Mobb
Deep</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-all_music_1-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-all_music-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="1998.E2.80.932005:_Signing_to_Atlantic_Records.2C_Terror_Squad.2C_feud_with_50_Cent">1998â€“2005:
Signing
to
Atlantic
Records,
Terror
Squad,
feud
with
50
Cent</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Fat_Joe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4"
title="Edit
section:
1998â€“2005:
Signing
to
Atlantic
Records,
Terror
Squad,
feud
with
50
Cent">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Released
in
1998,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Don_Cartagena?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Don
Cartagena">Don
Cartagena</a></i>
was
Joe's
third
album
and
his
first
for
Atlantic
Records.
It
peaked
on
The
Billboard
200
at
#7
and
#2
on
Top
R&amp;B/Hip
Hop
albums,
eventually
being
certified
gold
by
the
RIAA.<sup
id="cite_ref-riaa_cert_7-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-riaa_cert-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The
album
featured
two
hit
singles
&quot;Bet
Ya
Man
Can't
Triz&quot;,
and
&quot;Don
Cartagena&quot;.
Guest
appearances
included
<a
href="/wiki/Nas_(rapper)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nas
(rapper)"
class="mw-redirect">Nas</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Sean_Combs?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sean
Combs">Diddy</a>,
Big
Pun,
<a
href="/wiki/Raekwon?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Raekwon">Raekwon</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Jadakiss?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jadakiss">Jadakiss</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Bone_Thugs-N-Harmony?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bone
Thugs-N-Harmony"
class="mw-redirect">Bone
Thugs-N-Harmony</a>.
Within
the
album,
Fat
Joe
debuted
his
own
group
Terror
Squad
that
consisted
of
the
late
Big
Pun,
as
well
as
Cuban
Link,
Triple
Seis,
Prospect,
Armageddon
and
later
Remy
Ma.<sup
id="cite_ref-amg_terror_squad_8-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-amg_terror_squad-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup>
Joe
himself
acknowledged,
in
an
interview
with
HipHopGame.com,
that
he
has
received
criticism
for
releasing
only
one
solo
album
by
a
former
Terror
Squad
member,
Remy
Ma,
as
well
as
barely
featuring
original
members
Prospect
and
Armageddon
on
&quot;True
Story.&quot;
Terror
Squad
singer
Tony
Sunshine
has
had
possible
album
release
dates
pushed
back
over
three
years,
and
Joe
had
stated
that
artists
Prospect
and
Armageddon
have
not
released
solo
albums
yet
as
the
result
of
them
being
&quot;really
lazy&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-joecrack_9-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-joecrack-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup>
Former
Terror
Squad
member
Triple
Seis
also
went
on
record
when
asked
who
had
written
Fat
Joe's
lyrics,
stating
that
he
and
Pun
were
Joe's
ghostwriters,
and
asserts
that
Joe
continues
to
hire
ghostwriters.<sup
id="cite_ref-seis_10-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-seis-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1999,
he
appeared
on
<a
href="/wiki/Jennifer_Lopez?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jennifer
Lopez">Jennifer
Lopez</a>'s
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Feelin%27_So_Good?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Feelin'
So
Good">Feelin'
So
Good</a>&quot;
from
her
<i><a
href="/wiki/On_the_6?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="On
the
6">On
the
6</a></i>
album
with
late
rapper
Big
Pun.</p>








<p>Fat
Joe
released
his
fourth
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Jealous_Ones_Still_Envy_(J.O.S.E.)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jealous
Ones
Still
Envy
(J.O.S.E.)">Jealous
Ones
Still
Envy
(J.O.S.E.)</a></i>
in
2001,
featuring
production
from
the
then-popular
Irv
Gotti.
The
album
featured
a
star-studded
line
up
from
the
likes
of
Ashanti,
<a
href="/wiki/Ja_Rule?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ja
Rule">Ja
Rule</a>,
N.O.R.E.,
<a
href="/wiki/Busta_Rhymes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Busta
Rhymes">Busta
Rhymes</a>,
Petey
Pablo,
M.O.P.,
<a
href="/wiki/Ludacris?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ludacris">Ludacris</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/R._Kelly?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="R.
Kelly">R.
Kelly</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Buju_Banton?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Buju
Banton">Buju
Banton</a>,
and
artists
from
his
Terror
Squad
label.
The
lead
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/We_Thuggin%27?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="We
Thuggin'">We
Thuggin'</a>&quot;
featuring
R.
Kelly
was
a
big
hit
in
late
2001,
but
would
not
reach
the
level
of
the
Irv
Gotti-produced
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/What%27s_Luv%3F?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="What's
Luv?">What's
Luv?</a>&quot;
which
was
a
massive
hit
in
early
2002
and
featured
The
Inc.
superstars
<a
href="/wiki/Ja_Rule?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ja
Rule">Ja
Rule</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Ashanti_(entertainer)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ashanti
(entertainer)"
class="mw-redirect">Ashanti</a>.
The
album
was
Fat
Joe's
biggest
hit
as
it
was
successful
from
its
January
release
all
the
way
into
May,
being
certified
platinum.<sup
id="cite_ref-riaa_cert_7-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-riaa_cert-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup>
However,
Fat
Joe's
fifth
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Loyalty_(Fat_Joe_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Loyalty
(Fat
Joe
album)">Loyalty</a></i>,
released
later
in
2002
and
featuring
production
from
Irv
Gotti,
was
not
as
successful.</p>








<p>In
2003,
Fat
Joe
was
featured
in
the
pop
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/I_Want_You/Me_Pones_Sexy?qsrc=3044"

<a

The

Sunshine
performed
the

&quot;Crush
Tonight&quot;
from
<i>Loyalty</i>
on

<i><a

class="reference"><a

<p>Despite

in

&quot;<a

<a

for

However,
Jason

of
<a

&quot;a

<a

beat

<p>A

<i><a

Fat

&quot;I

<a

title="G-Unit">G-Unit</a>.&quot;<sup

<p><i><a
href="/wiki/Me,_Myself_%26_I_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Me,
Myself
&amp;
I
(album)">Me,
Myself
&amp;
I</a></i>,
released
in
2006,
is
Fat
Joe's
seventh
album.
It
was
his
first
album
released
on
his
new
deal
with
<a
href="/wiki/Virgin_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Virgin
Records">Virgin
Records</a>.
It
featured
the
hit
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Make_It_Rain?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Make
It
Rain">Make
It
Rain</a>&quot;
with
southern
rapper
<a
href="/wiki/Lil_Wayne?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lil
Wayne">Lil
Wayne</a>,
followed
by
&quot;No
Drama
(Clap
and
Revolve)&quot;.
Fat
Joe
did
a
freestyle
cipher
segment
for
<a
href="/wiki/VH1?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="VH1">VH1</a>'s
&quot;Freestyle
59&quot;
competition
in
October
2006
prior
to
the
VH1
Hip
Hop
Honors
featuring
New
Jersey
emcee
Neuse.<sup
id="cite_ref-25"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In

2007,

Michael

Joe
as
among

he

(record
label)"
class="mw-redirect">Terror
Squad</a>
imprint
to
the
<a

family

Browz">Ron

Kim">Lil'

<a

<a

<h3><span

<p>In
January
2010,

Joe
announced
that
he
was
working
on
a
new

<i><a

1">The
Darkside
Vol.
1</a></i>.

News
reported
that

Joe
intended
&quot;all
the

be
much
harsher&quot;
than
his
previous
album.

comes
from

<p>On

28,
2010
Fat
Joe
signed
a
record
deal
with
<a
href="/wiki/E1_Music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="E1
Music">E1
Music</a>.<sup

href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup><sup

title="The

Darkside
Vol.
1</a></i>
was

on

27,
2010
and
sold
approximately
12,000
copies
in
the
first
week
and
entered
the
Billboard
200
at
#27.</p>








<p>On
August
6,
2010
Fat
Joe
was
interviewed
on
MTV
RapFix
Live
by
Sway.
Fat
Joe
announced
in
the
interview
that
he
planned
to
record
2
more
volumes
of
<i>The
Darkside</i>
and
then
retire.<sup
id="cite_ref-40"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

(song)"

Brown</a>.<sup

<p>On

19,
2011

<h3><span

Family">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Fat
Joe
currently
lives
in
Miami
and
is
married
with
three
children.<sup

<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Community_work">Community
work</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Fat_Joe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17"

section:
Community
work">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Fat
Joe
has
been
back
to
his
old
school
in
the
Bronx,
New
York
to
donate
computers
for
the
students.</p>








<p>In
2008
He
attended
the
grand
opening
of
the
Hip
Hop
Soda
Shop
in
Miami
which
was
community
outreach
project
set
up
by
<a
href="/wiki/Benjamin_Chavis?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Benjamin
Chavis">Ben
Chavis</a>
for
the
youth
to
hang
out
and
do
things
such
as
record
music,
use
the
computers
and
play
on
Xbox
360s.<sup
id="cite_ref-45"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>At
a
&quot;School
is
Cool&quot;
assembly
in
<a
href="/wiki/Jersey_City_Public_Schools?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jersey
City
Public
Schools">Public
School
5</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/Jersey_City,_New_Jersey?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jersey
City,
New
Jersey">Jersey
City,
New
Jersey</a>
on
June
11,
2009,
Fat
Joe
was
a
speaker.<sup
id="cite_ref-46"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
January
23,
2011
Fat
Joe
appeared
with
<a
href="/wiki/Newark,_New_Jersey?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Newark,
New
Jersey">Newark</a>
mayor
<a
href="/wiki/Cory_Booker?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cory
Booker">Cory
Booker</a>
and
fitness
expert
<a
href="/wiki/Jeff_Halevy?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"

Halevy</a>
at
an

to

the
Newark
branch
of
<a
href="/wiki/Michelle_Obama?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Michelle
Obama">Michelle
Obama</a>'s
<i><a
href="/wiki/Let%27s_Move!?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"

Move!">Let's
Move!</a></i>
initiative
against
childhood
obesity.<sup

class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Weight_loss">Weight
loss</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Fat_Joe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18"
title="Edit
section:
Weight
loss">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>By
1996,
he
weighed
300
pounds
(140&nbsp;kg).<sup
id="cite_ref-Faithful_2-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Faithful-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
2005,
<i>Stuff</i>
magazine<sup
id="cite_ref-48"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
<i>ContactMusic.com</i><sup
id="cite_ref-49"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup>
profiled
Fat
Joe's
weight
loss
efforts.</p>








<p>In
2011,
Fat
Joe
unveiled
his
latest
weight
loss
efforts
in
the
video
for
his
song
&quot;Drop
a
Body&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-50"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup>
after
shedding
88
pounds
off
his
previous
weight
of
350
pounds.
He
has
said
although
he
loves
to
eat
KFC,
McDonaldâ€™s
and
other
less
healthy
foods
he
had
to
stop
due
to
losing
several
friends,
including
former
Terror
Squad
member
<a
href="/wiki/Big_Pun?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Big
Pun">Big
Pun</a>
to
obesity
and
he
wanted
to
stay
alive
to
see
his
children
grow
up.
He
lost
the
weight
without
the
help
of
supplements
and
fat
diets
by
combining
2-hour
cardio
and
weight
lifting
sessions
with
proper
eating
habits.
Instead
of
Burger
King,
KFC,
and
McDonaldâ€™s,
he
opted
for
smaller
portioned
meals
of
fruit,
vegetables,
and
lean
meats.<sup
id="cite_ref-51"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup>
Furthermore
he
follows
a
low-carb
approach,
eating
some
sweet
potatoes
but
not
eating
bread,
rice
and
pasta.<sup
id="cite_ref-52"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Legal_issues">Legal
issues</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Fat_Joe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19"
title="Edit
section:
Legal
issues">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>On
September
8,
1998,
Fat
Joe
and
Big
Pun
were
arrested
on
assault
charges
for
hitting
a
man
with
a
baseball
bat
and
stealing
the
man's
gold
chain
on
June
14
that
year.<sup
id="cite_ref-Different_Music_3-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Different_Music-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup>
Joe
was
arrested
again
on
May
12,
2002
for
allegedly
fighting
with
another
man
at
B.B.
King's
Blues
Club
in
<a
href="/wiki/Times_Square?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Times
Square">Times
Square</a>,
but
the
charges
were
dropped
on
January
10,
2003.<sup
id="cite_ref-53"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
two
murder
cases,
Fat
Joe
has
been
named
a
witness:</p>








<p>Joe's
former
bodyguard,
Jose
Mulero
(also
known
as
Sing
Sing),
was
arrested
on
September
17,
2004
for
the
April
15,
1994
shooting
death
of
16-year-old
Ernesto
Rivera
at
a
Bronx
nightclub.
Responding
to
a
<a
href="/wiki/Subpoena?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Subpoena">subpoena</a>,
Fat
Joe
claimed
to
have
heard
the
shooting
and
seen
people
fleeing
the
scene,
but
investigators
argued
that
he
was
standing
closer
to
Mulero,
by
a
door.<sup
id="cite_ref-54"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p><a
href="/wiki/Miami_Beach_Police_Department?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Miami
Beach
Police
Department">Miami
Beach
police</a>
also
named
Fat
Joe
as
a
witness
in
a
Memorial
Day
double
homicide
outside
David's
Cafe
II
in
<a
href="/wiki/South_Beach?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="South
Beach">South
Beach</a>.
Jermaine
<i>Wufgang</i>
Chamberline
of
<a
href="/wiki/Miami_Gardens?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Miami
Gardens"
class="mw-redirect">Miami
Gardens</a>
was
accused
of
shooting
Lessli
Paz
and
Joey
Navarro
to
death
on
that
morning;
Fat
Joe
and
the
two
victims
were
sitting
in
a
rented
<a
href="/wiki/Cadillac_Escalade?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cadillac
Escalade">Cadillac
Escalade</a>
parked
outside
the
restaurant
when
a
fight
broke
out
between
passengers
and
another
man.<sup
id="cite_ref-55"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
December
2012,
Fat
Joe
pled
guilty
to
<a
href="/wiki/Tax_evasion?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tax
evasion">tax
evasion</a>
for
not
paying
income
tax
on
over
3
million
dollars
from
2007-2010.
It
was
reported
he
could
face
up
to
two
years
in
prison
and
a
fine
of
up
to
$200,000,
plus
penalties
from
the
<a
href="/wiki/IRS?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="IRS"
class="mw-redirect">IRS</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-56"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
was
to
be
sentenced
during
April
2013.<sup
id="cite_ref-57"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
June
24,
2013,
he
was
sentenced
to
four
months
in
prison
for
tax
evasion.<sup
id="cite_ref-58"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
began
the
sentence
on
August
26,
2013,
and
was
released
on
November
28,
2013.<sup
id="cite_ref-59"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-60"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="LGBT_beliefs_and_support">LGBT
beliefs
and
support</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Fat_Joe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20"
title="Edit
section:
LGBT
beliefs
and
support">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>During
an
interview
with
<a
href="/wiki/DJ_Vlad?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="DJ
Vlad">Vlad
TV</a>,
Joe
stated
that
while
not
gay
himself,
gay
people
should
not
hide
their
sexuality
and
stand
by
what
they
are.
He
mentioned
that
it's
possible
that
he
has
done
songs
with
gay
rappers
and
that
there
are
likely
several
gay
people
besides
just
rappers
in
the
hip
hop
industry
who
are
in
the
closet,
describing
it
as
a
&quot;Gay
Mafia&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-61"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>His
comments
came
after
being
asked
to
comment
on
<a
href="/wiki/Mister_Cee?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mister
Cee">Mister
Cee</a>
being
arrested
for
public
lewdness
with
a
transgender.<sup
id="cite_ref-62"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<script
type="text/javascript">




render_ads(false,
window['ad_config_bot']);





function
afc_match()
{








var
count
=
-1;








if(window['ad_config_top'])
{












count
=
window['ad_config_top'];








}









var
countBottom
=
0;








if(window['ad_config_bot'])
{












countBottom
=
window['ad_config_bot'];








}









if(window['backfillParam'])
{




























window['backfillParam']['pl_bmodn']
=
5;
























window['backfillParam']['pl_tnum']
=
count;












window['backfillParam']['pl_bnum']
=
countBottom;








}


































var
_matchUrl
=
"/afc-match?q=Fat_Joe&page=1&ac=24&qid=A54F65E571E7DF6E699325CE2D875AB7&qsrc=121&dm=&qrt=2&lid="+
"&o=0&l=dir&oo=&cl=ca-aj-cat&ch=cx_ask_wiki,ad_dirN";





















_matchUrl+=
"&userip=76.78.3.114";




































_matchUrl+="&losid=a&locid=encw&lodid=us&loaid=a16";









var
location
=
window.location
+
"";








location
=
location.substring(7);








var
cutIdx
=
location.indexOf("/");








if
(location.indexOf(":")
>
-1)
{




















cutIdx
=
1
+
cutIdx
+
location.substring(cutIdx+1).indexOf("/");








}









var
urlPrefix
=
location.substring(0,
cutIdx);








_matchUrl
=
"http://"
+
urlPrefix
+
_matchUrl
+
"&afcec="
+
count
+
"&afcecb="
+
countBottom;








ajax_get(_matchUrl,
null,
null);




}





function
getXHR()
{








if
(window.XMLHttpRequest)
{












return
new
XMLHttpRequest();








}
else
if
(window.ActiveXObject)
{












try
{
















return
new
ActiveXObject("Msxml2.XMLHTTP");












}
catch
(e)
{
















try
{




















return
new
ActiveXObject("Microsoft.XMLHTTP");
















}
catch
(E)
{




















return
null;
















}












}








}








else
{












return
null;








}




}





function
ajax_get(url,
onsuccess,
onerror)
{








var
obj
=
getXHR();








if(obj)
{












obj.onreadystatechange
=
function()
{
















if(obj.readyState==4)
{




















if
(obj.status
==
200
&&
typeof(onsuccess)
==
"function")
{
























onsuccess(obj);




















}
else
if
(typeof(onerror)
==
"function")
{
























onerror(obj);




















}






















try
{
























delete
obj['onreadystatechange'];




















}
catch(e)
{}
















}












};












obj.open("GET",
url,
true,
"",
"");












obj.send(null);












return
obj;








}
else
{












if(onerror)
{
















onerror("Error
creating
XHR");












}
else
{
















a10.debug("Error
creating
XHR");












}












return
null;








}




}





afc_match();

</script>
